Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 2/31
Simple Linear Regression
A statistical tool that helps make data-based and informative decisions
Managerial decisions often are based on the relationship between two
or more variables
Stock price & crude oil price
Tariff tax and inflation rate
Insurance co-pay and # of students at a university
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 3/31
Simple Linear Regression
Regression analysis can be used to develop anequation(aka. model)
showing how multiple variables(2+) are related.
Regression analysis is used to:
Predict the value of a dependent variable based on the value of at least
one independent variable
Explain the impact of changes in an independent variable on the
dependent variable
Dependent variable(y): the variable we wish to predict or explain
Independent variable(xi): the variable(s) used to explain the
dependent variable
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 4/31
Simple Linear Regression
Simple linear regression involves one independent variable and one
dependent variable.
The relationship between the two variables is approximated by a
straight line.
Regression analysis involving two or more independent variables is
called multiple regression.
In the future, you will see multivariate and multiple linear
regression(one dependent variable and multiple independent variables)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 5/31
Correlation vs. Regression
Correlation
Correlation measures the strength and direction of the linear
relationship between two variables.
It is quantified by the correlation coefficient which ranges from -1 to
+1, with 0 indicating no linear relationship.
Correlation is only concerned with the strength of the relationship
between variables;it does not infer causality or dependence.
A high correlation between study hours and test scores does not imply
that studying causes higher scores, as other factors may be involved.
Regression
Regression goes beyond measuring the strength of the relationship and
models the nature of the relationship between a dependent variabley
and one or more independent variablesxi
Regression implies causality when the model assumptions are met, as it
attempts to explain how changes inxi influence y
Example: Using regression, you can predict sales revenuey based on
advertising expenditure x
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 6/31
Simple Linear Regression Model
Simple linear regression only has one independent variabley
The linear equation that describes howy is related tox and an error
term is called the regression model
Changes in y are assumed to be caused by changes inx
The simple linear regression model is
y =β0 +β1x +ϵ
Where: β0 and β1 are the parameters of the model.ϵis a random variable
called the error term.

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 25/31
Some Discussion
y =β0 +β1x is just A model, not THE model
This is the starting point, or a baseline model that helps you get
started on the optimization/refinement process
Later, you will have to add the error term(aka.ϵ) to the equation to
find the most accurate/optimized model that represents the entire
dataset the best
It’s okay to just usey =β0 +β1x to do some basic and intuitive
predictions.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 26/31
Model Evaluation
You will be learning a lot in the Machine Learning and Data Science
classes
Many techniques can be used to evaluate different linear regression
models
All have pros and cons
Depending on the problems you are working with, trade-offs have to be
evaluated
Some very common approaches
Model fitness approach
Statistical approach
Assumption checking approach
Prediction accuracy
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 27/31
Model Evaluation - Goodness of Fit
1 R 2(Coefficient of Determination)
Measures the proportion of variance in the dependent variable
explained by the model
Ranges from 0 to 1; higher values indicate a better fit
2 Residual Standard Error (RSE):
Measures the average distance between observed values and the
regression line
Lower RSE indicates a better fit
3 And many more...
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 28/31
Model Evaluation - Statistical Approach
1 p-values of Coefficients
Tests if predictors significantly influence the response variable.
p-value < 0.05 indicates significance (commonly used threshold).
2 F-statistic
Tests the overall significance of the model.
A large F-statistic and a small p-value suggest that you have
developed a good model
3 And many more...
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 29/31
Model Evaluation - Assumption Checking Approach
Note to the assumptions
Error and residual share the same idea, BUT
An error is a deviation from the population mean.
A residual is a deviation from the sample mean.
4 Assumptions(More explanation will be given later in the Data
Science class)
Linearity: The relationship between predictorsx and response y must
be linear.
Independence of errors: There is not a relationship between the
residuals and they variable; in other words,y is independent of errors.
Normality of errors: The residuals must be approximately normally
distributed.
Equal Variances(Homoscedasticity): Variance of residuals should
remain constant, which means that the variance of the residuals is the
same for all values ofx.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 30/31
Model Evaluation - Prediction Accuracy
It’s too naive to just look at the model prediction accuracy
A lot of people focus too much on model prediction accuracy, which is
not professional. Remember the doctors making Type-I and Type-II
Errors?
Is Star Wars better than Star Trek?
It’s a very important approach, but it should NOT be used as the
only approach to evaluate the model performance:
1 Just a % = Correct Outcomes
All Possible Outcomes
Mean Absolute Error (MAE): Average absolute difference between
observed and predicted values.
Mean Squared Error (MSE): Average squared difference between
observed and predicted values.
Root Mean Squared Error (RMSE): Square root of MSE; indicates
typical prediction error.
And many more...
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/23/2025 31/31

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 3 / 23
Introduction
In this chapter, we study continuous random variables and discuss
THREE continuous probability distributions:
The continuous uniform,
The exponential,
The normal.
Because of its wide applicability and its extensive use in statistical
inference in business management, economics and engineering, the
normal distribution is the big boss.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 4 / 23
Introduction
Probabilities are computed differently for discrete and continuous
random variables.
With discrete random variables, the probability functionf (x ) provides
the probability that the random variable assumes a particular value.
With continuous random variables,
The probability that x assumes a particular value is zero, and a value in
a given interval is the corresponding area under the graph of f (x );
f (x ) is called the Probability Density Function(PDF).
Continuous probability distribution: A probability distribution in which
the continuous random variablex can take on any value, and there are
infinite values that X could assume.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 5 / 23
Why Called PDF?
What’s the area of a square?
What’s the area of a rectangle?
What’s the area of a circle?
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 6 / 23
Why Called PDF?
What’s the area of the following shape?
Figure 1: A Weird Continuous Distribution
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 7 / 23
Continuous Uniform Distribution
A random variable is described by a uniform probability distribution
whenever the probability is proportional to the interval’s length.
In English, The probability density function for the continuous uniform
distribution is constant across the entire range.
The uniform probability density function is:
f (x ) =
{ 1
b−a for a≤x≤b
0 elsewhere (1)
Where
a = smallest value the variablex can assume
b = largest value the variablex can assume
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 8 / 23
Continuous Uniform Distribution Examples
New Product Pricing : When a company launches a new product and
has limited historical pricing data, it might assume that the acceptable
price range to consumers is uniformly distributed. For example, if the
company believes consumers will pay between $50 and $100 for the
product, every price within this range is considered equally likely
until further market research is conducted .
Demand Forecasting During a Limited-Time Event : For events
with little historical data, such as the annual sale of a small business,
the expected sales per day could be modeled as uniformly distributed
within a reasonable range, assuming each day of the event is equally
promoted and accessible.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 9 / 23
Uniform Distribution
For an uniform continuous probability distribution
The expected value is:
E (x ) = a + b
2
The variance is:
Var(x ) = (b−a)2
12
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 10 / 23
Area as a Measure of Probability
The flight time of an airplane traveling from Chicago to New York can
be described by a continuous random variable
The historic data shows that all non-delayed flights take 120 to 140
minutes.
The flight time is uniformly distributed between 120 and 140 minutes.
That is, the probability of the flight time being within any 1-minute
interval between 120 and 140 minutes is equal for each minute.
Thus, the random variablex is said to have the following uniform
probability distribution.
f (x ) =
{ 1
140−120 for 120≤x≤140
0 elsewhere (2)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/17/2025 11 / 23
Area as a Measure of Probability
What is the probability that the flight time is between 120 and 130

Exponential Probability Distribution

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/25/2024 4/21
Introduction
A point estimator is a sample statistic used to estimate a population
parameter.
The sample mean¯x is a point estimator of the population meanµand
the sample proportionˆp is a point estimator of the population
proportion p
The sampling distributions of¯x and ˆp play key roles in computing
these interval estimates.
An interval estimateis computed by adding and subtracting a
value(called the margin of error) to the point estimate. Thus, the
general forms of an interval estimate of a population mean and
proportion are:
¯x ±Margin of Error and ˆp ±Margin of Error
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/25/2024 5/21
Margin of Error and the Interval Estimate
A point estimatorcannot be expected to provide the exact value of
the population parameter.
But we want to try hard to get closer and closer
An interval estimatecan be computed by adding and subtracting a
margin of error to the point estimate.
The purpose of an interval estimate is to provide information about
how close the point estimate is to the value of the parameter.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/25/2024 6/21
Interval Estimate of a Population Mean:σ Known
In order to develop an interval estimate of a population mean, the
margin of error must be computed using either:
The population standard deviationσ, or
The sample standard deviations
σis rarely KNOWN exactly(why?). But often a good estimate can be
obtained based on historical data and/or other information available
We refer to such cases as theσKNOWN case
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/25/2024 7/21

Let us construct an interval estimate ofµ, the mean amount spent
per shopping trip for the population of Lloyd’s customers, in a case
for which it is reasonable to treatσas known, given:
n = 100 customers, a simple random sample
x = the amount spent per shopping trip
s = 20, based on historical data
The population follows a normal distribution
Calculations reveal that the sample mean
a point estimate of population meanµ, is: ¯x = $82.

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/25/2024 20/21
Practical Advice(You May Get Asked by An
Interviewer)
Adequate Sample Size
The sampling distribution of¯x is normal if the underlying population
distribution is normal; otherwise, a sample size ofn≥30 is required.
If the population distribution is highly skewed or contains outliers, a
sample size of 50 or more is recommended.
If the population is not normally distributed but is roughly symmetric,
a sample size as small as 15 will suffice.
If the population is believed to be at least approximately normal, a
sample size of less than 15 can be used.
For small sample sizes, a histogram of the sample data should be built
to learn about the shape of the population distribution.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/25/2024 21/21

What is Hypothesis Testing? And Why Do We
Need It?
We have to make guesses/predictions all the time with very limited
information
Some are right and some are wrong
2 types of wrong answers
Set up theSTATISTICALboundaries for the guess
If your guess is within the boundaries, it’s anacceptable(correct)
guess
If your guess if out of the boundaries, it’s a false/wrong guess
Hypothesis testing is the mathematical representation of those
boundaries
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 4/45
Hypothesis Testing
Hypothesis testing can be used to determine whether a statement
about the value of a population parameter
Should or should not be rejected
Believed to be true or false
The null hypothesis, denoted byH0 , is atentative assumption about
a population parameter
The alternative hypothesis, denoted byHa or H1, is the opposite of
what is stated in the null hypothesis
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 5/45
To-Do’s for Hypothesis Testing
Step 1: grab some sample data from a population
Step 2: use some data from a sample to test the twocompeting
statements
Indicated by H0 and Ha
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 6/45
Developing Null and Alternative Hypotheses
It could be tricky to understand the context of the situation and
structure the hypotheses appropriately so that the test conclusion
provides the desired information.
All hypothesis testing applications involvecollecting a sampleand
using the sample results to provide evidence for drawing a conclusion.
Good questions to consider when formulating the null and alternative
hypotheses are:
What is the purpose of collecting the sample?
What conclusions are we hoping to make?
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 7/45
Developing Null and Alternative Hypotheses -
Example
When an attempt is being made to gather evidence in support of a
hypothesis, it is often best to begin with the alternative hypothesis
and make it the conclusion that the researcher hopes to support.
The conclusion that the research hypothesis is true is made if the
sample data provide sufficient evidence to show that the null
hypothesis can be rejected.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 8/45
An Example
Ford Motors is developing a new fuel injection that is believed to
provide an MPG of more than 24 MPG for their F-150’s.
We set the population mean miles per gallonHa :µ>24 as the
alternative hypothesis
And set the null hypothesis asH0 :µ≤24
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 9/45
Developing Null and Alternative Hypotheses
We might begin with a belief or assumption that a statement about
the value of a population parameter is true.
We then use a hypothesis test to challenge the assumption and
determine if there is statistical evidence to conclude that the
assumption is not true
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 10/45
Another Example
The label on an Ozarka water bottle states that it contains 16.9 fluid
ounces.
We assume the label correct
We assume the population mean filling weight,µ, is 16.9 fluid ounces,
We set it as the null hypothesis, orH0 :µ= 16.9
Then, we challenge the assumption in the alternative hypothesis
Ha :µ̸= 16.9
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 11/45
Summary of Forms for Null and Alternative
Hypotheses
Rule 1: The equality part of the hypotheses always appears in the null
hypothesis.
Rule 2: A hypothesis test about the value of a population meanµ
must take one of the followingTHREE forms, where # is the
hypothesized value of the population mean.
One-tailed (Lower-tail): H0 :µ≥# vs. Ha :µ<#
One-tailed (Upper-tail): H0 :µ≤# vs. Ha :µ>#
Two-tailed (Both Upper and Lower):H0 :µ= # vs. Ha :µ̸= #
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 12/45
Summary of Forms for Null and Alternative
Hypotheses
One-tailed (Lower-tail): H0 :µ≥# vs. Ha :µ<#
One-tailed (Upper-tail): H0 :µ≤# vs. Ha :µ>#
Two-tailed (Both Upper and Lower):H0 :µ= # vs. Ha :µ̸= #
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 13/45
Summary of Forms for Null and Alternative
Hypotheses
In this chapter, we show how statistical inference from sample data
and results can be used together with hypothesis testing to determine
whether a statement about thevalue of a population parameter
should or should not be rejected.
We quantify thefavor or support, if the sample results support or
favorite Ha,
Case1: We rejectH0 -> We supportH1
Case2: We do not rejectH0 -> We cannot supportH1
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 14/45
We Are Humans, We Make Mistakes/Wrong
Guesses.
Because hypothesis tests are based on sample data, we must allow for
the possibility of errors.
There are two types of error that can be made in hypothesis tests:
Type I and Type II errors.
Figure 1: Error Types
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 15/45
Type I and Type II Errors
Figure 2: Error Types
Figure 3: Correct Predictions and
Error Types
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 16/45
Type I and Type II Errors
Type I Error
A Type I error is rejectingH0 when it is true.
The probability of making a Type I error when the null hypothesis is
true as an equality is called the level of significance.
Applications of hypothesis testing that only control for the Type I error
are often called significance tests.
Type II Error
A Type II error is acceptingH0 when it is false.
Statisticians themselves avoid the risk of making a Type II error by
using “do not rejectH0” rather than “acceptH0”. - SNEAKY!!
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 17/45
Example of Type I and Type II Errors
Recall the hypothesis testing example about the new fuel injection
unit. Imagine you’ve developed a new fuel system for cars, and you
believe it makes cars more fuel-efficient than the current standard.
You decide to test if this new system really improves the car’s miles
per gallon (MPG) rating compared to the usual 24 MPG benchmark.
H0 :µ≤24
Ha :µ>24 (1)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 18/45
Example of Type I and Type II Errors
Type I Error: This is like sounding a false alarm.
It’s when youconclude that your new fuel system does indeed improve
the car’s MPG (makes it better than 24 MPG), but in reality, it doesn’t
— It’s just the same as the old system. So, youmistakenly think
you’ve made an improvement when you haven’t
Type II Error: This is like missing something important.
It’s when you decide that your new fuel system doesn’t make any
difference (so, MPG is 24 or less)
But in fact, it actually does improve the MPG. So, you’ve overlooked a
real improvement, thinking your system didn’t make the car more
fuel-efficient when it really did.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 19/45
Example of Type I and Type II Errors
In summary, a Type I error is thinking you’ve achieved something
special when you haven’t, and a Type II error is failing to recognize an
actual achievement, thinking nothing has changed.
Type I Error: Thinking your new system works (improves MPG) when
it doesn’t.
Type II Error: Not realizing your new system works (actually improves
MPG) when it does.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 20/45
One-Tailed Test About a Population Mean
One-tailed tests about a population mean take one of the following
two forms.
Lower/Left-Tailed Test
H0 :µ≥#
Ha :µ<# (2)
One-tailed tests about a population mean take one of the following
two forms.
Upper/Right-Tailed Test
H0 :µ≤#
Ha :µ># (3)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 21/45
One-Tailed Test About a Population Mean -
Example
Consider the example of the Federal Trade Commission (FTC) testing
a Hilltop Coffee’s claim that its large can contains at least 3 pounds
of coffee.
The FTC assumes Hilltop Coffee’s claim to be correct (µ≥3 pounds)
and sets the alternative hypothesis to challenge the claim, using the
lower tail test,µ<3 pounds. Thus, we write:
H0 :µ≥3
Ha :µ<3 (4)
The FTC is willing to take a 1% risk of making an error on its testing
of Hilltop Coffee’s claim.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 22/45

mean ¯x is computed as an estimate of the population meanµ.
Also, previous FTC tests show that the population of filling weights
can be assumed normally distributed with a known standard deviation
of valueσ= 0.18
We can write the sampling distribution of¯x as normally distributed,
centered around the hypothesized mean,µ=µ0 = 3, and with
standard error:
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 23/45

For the test statistic of a hypothesis test about a population mean:σ
known, we can use the standard normal random variable,z. Formally,
we write:

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 24/45
p-Value Approach to a Lower Tail Test About a
Population Mean: σ Known
A p-value is a probability, computed using the test statistic, that
measures the support provided by the sample for the null hypothesis.
Suppose the sample ofn = 36 coffee cans revealed¯x = 2.92 pounds.
Then, the test statistic is
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 25/45
p-Value Approach to a Lower Tail Test About a
Population Mean: σ Known
For a lower tail test, the p-value is the probability thatz is less than
or equal to−2.67.
p−value = P(z≤−2.67) = 0.0038
This p-value indicates a small probability of obtaining a sample mean
of ¯x = 2.92 or smaller when sampling from a population withµ= 3.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 26/45
Rejection Rule Option 1: Using p-Value
In the previous slide, we concluded that the calculated p-value does
not provide much support for the null hypothesis, **but is it small
enough to cause us to rejectH0? *
The answerdepends upon the level of significanceαfor the test:
If a p-value is less than or equal to the level of significanceα, the value
of the test statistic is in the rejection region.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 27/45
Rejection Rule Option 1: Using p-Value
Because the FTC stated to be willing to take a 1% risk of making a
Type I error, we set the significance levelα= 0.01.
We write the rejection rule using the p-value as:
Reject H0 if p-value≤α
With the p-value = 0.0038 being less than or equal toα= 0.01, we
reject H0.
Therefore, the FTC finds sufficient statistical evidence to conclude at
the 0.01 level of significance that the filling weight of Hilltop Coffee
cans is less than 3 pounds.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 28/45
Rejection Rule Option 2: Using Critical Value
We can use the standard normal probability distribution to find thez
value with an area ofαin the lower (or upper) tail of the distribution.
The value of the test statistic that establishes the boundary of the
rejection region is called the critical value for the test.
The rejection rule for a one-tailed test using the critical value is:
Lower Tail: RejectH0 if z≤zα
Upper Tail: RejectH0 if z≥zα
zαis such thatP(z≤zα) =α.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 29/45
Rejection Rule Option 2: Using Critical Value
In the Hilltop Coffee case, whenα= 0.01, zα=−2.33.
The rejection rule for a lower tail test becomes
Reject H0 if z≤−2.33, and becausez =−2.67, we rejectH0.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 30/45
Two-Tailed Test About a Population Mean
A two-tailed test about a population mean takes the following form.
H0 :µ=µ0
Ha :µ̸=µ0
(5)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 31/45
Two-Tailed Test About a Population Mean -
Example
Consider MaxFlight’s need of testing its manufacturing process to
ensure it produces golf balls with a mean driving distance of 295 yards.
If the golf balls drive less than 295 yards, MaxFlight will eventually lose
sales, and if the golf balls’ driving distance exceeds 295 yards, they may
be rejected by the USGA.
Thus, we assume that the mean driving distance is as specified by
MaxFlight, and challenge it in the alternative hypothesis, by writing:
H0 :µ= 295
Ha :µ̸= 295 (6)
The quality control team selectedα= 0.05 as the level of significance
for the test.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 32/45
Two-Tailed Test About a Population Mean -
Example
Suppose a sample ofn = 50 golf balls is collected, and the sample
mean ¯x = 297.6 is computed as an estimate of the population mean
µ.
Data from previous tests conducted when the process was known to
be in adjustment show that the population standard deviation can be
assumed known with a value ofσ= 12 (This isσknown case).
The sampling distribution of¯x as normally distributed, centered
around the hypothesized mean,µ=µ0 = 295, and with standard
error,σ¯x = σ√n = 1.7
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 33/45
Two-Tailed Test About a Population Mean -
Example
We write the test statistic of a hypothesis test about a population
mean: σknown, using the standard normal random variable,z, as:
z = ¯x−µ0
σ¯x
= 297.6−295
1.7 = 1.53
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 34/45
Two-Tailed Test About a Population Mean -
Example
The p-value corresponds to the probability of finding a value for z
that is at least as unlikely asz = 1.53.
For a two-tailed test of a symmetric sampling distribution, values of
z≥1.53 are just as unlikely as values ofz≤−1.53. Thus, we can
write the p-value as:
p-value = p(z≥1.53) + p(z≤−1.53)
Because the normal distribution is symmetric, we can calculate the
p-value as
p-value = p(z≥1.53) + p(z≤−1.53) = 0.0630 +0.0630 = 0.126
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 35/45
Two-Tailed Test About a Population Mean -
Example
Next, we apply the rejection rule:
Because p-value= 0.126> 0.05
(The quality control team selectedα= 0.05 as the level of significance
for the test.)
We cannot rejectH0.
Thus, no action will be taken to adjust the MaxFlight’s manufacturing
process.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/12/2024 36/45
Rejection Rule Using Critical Value for a Two-Tailed
Test
The rejection rule for a two-tailed test using the critical value is:
Reject H0 if z≤−zα/2 or z≥zα/2
In the golf ball case, we haveα= 0.05.
Thus, α/2 = 0.025, andzα/2 = z0.025 = 1.96
The rejection rule for this two-tail test becomes
Reject H0 if z≤−1.96 or z≥1.96
Because the value of the test statistic for the golf ball study is
z = 1.53, the statistical evidence willNOT permit us to reject the null
hypothesis at the 0.05 level of significance.

s/√n

Question 1
According to the Internal Revenue Service (IRS), individuals filing federal income tax returns prior to March
31 received an average refund of $1056 in 2018. Consider the population of “last-minute” filers who mail
their tax return during the last five days of the income tax period (typically April 10 to April 15).
a. A researcher suggests that a reason individuals wait until the last five days is that on average these
individuals receive lower refunds than do early filers. Develop appropriate hypotheses such that
rejection ofH0 will support the researcher’s contention.
b. For a sample of 400 individuals who filed a tax return between April 10 and 15, the sample mean
refund was $910. Based on prior experience a population standard deviation ofσ= $1, 600 may be
assumed. What is the p-value?
c. Atα= 0.05, what is your conclusion?
d. Repeat the preceding hypothesis test using the critical value approach.

Question 2

determine if it can be concluded that the mean credit card balance for undergraduate students has continued
to increase compared to the original report. Based on previous studies, use a population standard deviation
σ= $1, 000.

balance of $3,325?

number of texts for 25–34 year olds differs from the population daily mean number of texts for 18–24
year olds.

Normal Probability Distribution
The normal/Gaussian probability distribution is the most common
probability continuous distribution.
It’s used in a wide variety of practical applications.
It is widely applied to statistical inference
Something we will be using all the time from now on
The normal distribution assumes the classic bell-shaped curve and
provides a description of the likely results obtained through sampling.
We will talk about sampling next week.
Derived and proved by Abraham de Moivre, a French mathematician.
Work published on The Doctrine of Chances in 1733.
Same year the Molasses Act was imposed
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/19/2024 2 / 32
Normal Probability Density Function
The normal probability density function is described by two parameters:
the meanµand the standard deviationσ.
Don’t write it down. Too much work! ;)
f (x ) = 1
σ
√
2πe− 1
2 ( x −µ
σ )2
(1)
Where
π= 3.14159
e = 2.71828 - Euler’s Nmebr
Figure 1: Normal DistributionIan Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/19/2024 3 / 32
The Mean of the Normal Distribution
We make the following observations about the meanµof the normal
distribution:
1 The meanµis the highest point on the normal curve.
2 The meanµis also the median and mode of the distribution.
3 The mean of the distribution can be any numerical value: negative, zero,
or positive.
4 The normal distribution or the bell-shaped curve is symmetric.
5 The area under the curve to the left of the mean and the area under the
curve to the right of the mean are both 0.50.
6 The tails of the normal curve extend to infinity in both directions and
theoretically never touch the horizontal axis.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/19/2024 4 / 32

The Spread of the Normal Distribution
We make the following observations about the standard deviationσof
the normal distribution:
1 The standard deviation determines how flat and wide the normal curve is.
2 Larger values ofσresult in wider, flatter curves, showing more variability
in the data.
The figure shows two normal distributions with the same mean butσ=
5 andσ=10.
3 The mean determines the location of the curve, SD determines the
shape of the curve.

Standard Normal Probability Distribution
We need a tool to help us unify or convert these non-standard normal
distributions to a standard normal distribution.
A random variable having a normal distribution witha mean of 0 and
a standard deviation of 1 is said to have a standard normal
probability distribution.
The standard normal distribution has the same general appearance as
other normal distributions, but with the special properties of having
µ= 0 andσ= 1
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/19/2024 10 / 32

probability density function is a simpler version of the equation shown
earlier for the general normal probability distribution:

Standard Normal Probability Distribution
As with other continuous random variables, probability calculations
with a normal distribution are made by computing the area under the
graph of the normal curve over a given interval.
We will now show how to use the Z-Table to calculate the following
cumulative probabilities associated with a standard normal probability
distribution
The probability that the standard normal random variablez will be less
than or equal to a given valueZ: P(z≤Z1)
The probability thatz will be between two given values,
Z1 and Z2 : P(Z1≤z≤Z2)
The probability thatz will be greater than or equal to a given value
P(z≥Z2)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/19/2024 14 / 32

The probability that the standard normal random variablez will be less
than or equal to a given valueZ1: P(z≤Z1)
The probability thatz will be between two given values,
Z1 and Z2 : P(Z1≤z≤Z2)
The probability thatz will be greater than or equal to a given value
P(z≥Z2)

Cumulative Probability for P(z≤1.00)
The cumulative probability thatz is less than or equal to 1.00, that is,
P(z≤1.00), is the area under the standard normal curve to the left of
z = 1.00
To find the cumulative probability corresponding toz≤1.00 in the
Z-Table,
We identify the value located at the intersection of the row labeled 1.0
and the column labeled 0.00.
We find 1.0 in the left column of the table
We find 0.00 in the top row of the table.

Cumulative Probability for P(−0.50≤z≤1.25)
Three steps are required to compute this probability using the Z-Table
1 We calculate P(z≤−0.50) as the intersection of the –0.5 row and the
0.00 column:
P(z≤−0.50) = 0.3085
2 We calculate P(Z≤1.25) as the intersection of the 1.2 row and the
0.05 column:
P(z≤1.25) = 0.8944
3 We calculate the difference of the cumulative probabilities to the left of
z = 1.25 and z =−0.50 that we calculated in steps 1 and 2, so that:
P(−0.50≤z≤1.25) = P(z≤1.25)−P(z≤−0.50) = 0.5859
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 03/19/2024 19 / 32
Cumulative Probability for P(z≥1.58)
The cumulative probability thatz is greater than or equal to 1.58, that
is, P(z≥1.58), is the area under the standard normal curve to the
right of z = 1.58.
To find the probability to the right ofz = 1.58, we need to first find
the probability corresponding to the left ofz = 1.58, and then
calculate its complement.
To calculate the area to the left ofz = 1.58, identify the value located
at the intersection of the row labeled 1.5 and the column labeled 0.08.
Thus, P(z≤1.58) = 0.9429

P(z≤z ∗) = 1−P(z≥z ∗) = 1−0.10 = 0.90

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 2/31
Simple Linear Regression
A statistical tool that helps make data-based and informative decisions
Managerial decisions often are based on the relationship between two
or more variables
Stock price & crude oil price
Tariff tax and inflation rate
Insurance co-pay and # of students at a university
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 3/31
Simple Linear Regression
Regression analysis can be used to develop anequation(aka. model)
showing how multiple variables(2+) are related.
Regression analysis is used to:
Predict the value of a dependent variable based on the value of at least
one independent variable
Explain the impact of changes in an independent variable on the
dependent variable
Dependent variable(y): the variable we wish to predict or explain
Independent variable(xi): the variable(s) used to explain the
dependent variable
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 4/31
Simple Linear Regression
Simple linear regression involves one independent variable and one
dependent variable.
The relationship between the two variables is approximated by a
straight line.
Regression analysis involving two or more independent variables is
called multiple regression.
In the future, you will see multivariate and multiple linear regression(one
dependent variable and multiple independent variables)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 5/31
Correlation vs. Regression
Correlation
Correlation measures the strength and direction of the linear relationship
between two variables.
It is quantified by the correlation coefficient which ranges from -1 to +1,
with 0 indicating no linear relationship.
Correlation is only concerned with the strength of the relationship
between variables;it does not infer causality or dependence.
A high correlation between study hours and test scores does not imply
that studying causes higher scores, as other factors may be involved.
Regression
Regression goes beyond measuring the strength of the relationship and
models the nature of the relationship between a dependent variabley
and one or more independent variablesxi
Regression implies causality when the model assumptions are met, as it
attempts to explain how changes inxi influence y
Example: Using regression, you can predict sales revenuey based on
advertising expenditure x
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 6/31
Simple Linear Regression Model
Simple linear regression only has one independent variabley
The linear equation that describes howy is related tox and an error
term is called the regression model
Changes in y are assumed to be caused by changes inx
The simple linear regression model is
y =β0 +β1x +ϵ
Where: β0 and β1 are the parameters of the model.ϵis a random variable
called the error term.

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 25/31
Some Discussion
y =β0 +β1x is just A model, not THE model
This is the starting point, or a baseline model that helps you get started
on the optimization/refinement process
Later, you will have to add the error term(aka.ϵ) to the equation to
find the most accurate/optimized model that represents the entire
dataset the best
It’s okay to just usey =β0 +β1x to do some basic and intuitive
predictions.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 26/31
Model Evaluation
You will be learning a lot in the Machine Learning and Data Science
classes
Many techniques can be used to evaluate different linear regression
models
All have pros and cons
Depending on the problems you are working with, trade-offs have to be
evaluated
Some very common approaches
Model fitness approach
Statistical approach
Assumption checking approach
Prediction accuracy
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 27/31
Model Evaluation - Goodness of Fit
1 R 2(Coefficient of Determination)
Measures the proportion of variance in the dependent variable
explained by the model
Ranges from 0 to 1; higher values indicate a better fit
2 Residual Standard Error (RSE):
Measures the average distance between observed values and the
regression line
Lower RSE indicates a better fit
3 And many more...
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 28/31
Model Evaluation - Statistical Approach
1 p-values of Coefficients
Tests if predictors significantly influence the response variable.
p-value < 0.05 indicates significance (commonly used threshold).
2 F-statistic
Tests the overall significance of the model.
A large F-statistic and a small p-value suggest that you have developed
a good model
3 And many more...
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 29/31
Model Evaluation - Assumption Checking Approach
Note to the assumptions
Error and residual share the same idea, BUT
An error is a deviation from the population mean.
A residual is a deviation from the sample mean.
4 Assumptions(More explanation will be given later in the Data Science
class)
Linearity: The relationship between predictorsx and response y must be
linear.
Independence of errors: There is not a relationship between the residuals
and the y variable; in other words,y is independent of errors.
Normality of errors: The residuals must be approximately normally
distributed.
Equal Variances(Homoscedasticity): Variance of residuals should remain
constant, which means that the variance of the residuals is the same for
all values ofx.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 30/31
Model Evaluation - Prediction Accuracy
It’s too naive to just look at the model prediction accuracy
A lot of people focus too much on model prediction accuracy, which is
not professional. Remember the doctors making Type-I and Type-II
Errors?
Is Star Wars better than Star Trek?
It’s a very important approach, but it should NOT be used as the only
approach to evaluate the model performance:
1 Just a % = Correct Outcomes
All Possible Outcomes
Mean Absolute Error (MAE): Average absolute difference between
observed and predicted values.
Mean Squared Error (MSE): Average squared difference between
observed and predicted values.
Root Mean Squared Error (RMSE): Square root of MSE; indicates
typical prediction error.
And many more...
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/21/2024 31/31

Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 2/41
Measures of Variability
For example
In choosing supplier A or supplier B we might consider not only the
average delivery time for each, but also the variability in delivery time for
each.
Supplier A promises to deliver a shipment every 10 days, and has never
missed or delayed a shipment in the past year.
Supplier B promises to deliver a shipment every 3 days, but havs missed
or delayed more than half of the previous shipments.
Which stock to buy? NVDA or COST?
Common tool to measure the variability are:
Range
Interquartile Range
Variance
Standard Deviation
And more...
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 3/41
Why Do We Want To Know the Variability?
This is a crazy world generating crazy datasets all the time!
A dataset with big variability could lead to messy/misleading/wrong
conclusions
We want to use tools to identify if any variability exists in the dataset
If yes, how much?
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 4/41
Range
The range of a data set is the difference between the largest and
smallest data value.
It is the simplest measure of variability.
It is very sensitive to the smallest and largest data values.
Range = largest value−smallest value = 715−525 = 190.
Figure 1: Rent Example - Range
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 5/41
Interquartile Range (IQR)
The interquartile range of a dataset is the difference between thethird
quartile and thefirst quartile.
It is the range for the middle 50% of the data (75% - 25%).
It overcomes the sensitivity to extreme data values.
Figure 2: IQR Rent Example
3rd Quartile (Q3) = 625
1st Quartile (Q1) = 545
IQR = 625 – 545 = 80
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 6/41
What Does An IQR of 80 Mean?
The IQR is the range between the first quartile (25th percentile) and
the third quartile (75th percentile) of the dataset.
An IQR of 80 means that the middle 50% of your data is spread out
over a range of 80 units.
Robustness to Outliers: Unlike range, which considers the extreme
values, the IQR focuses on the central part of the dataset and is less
influenced by outliers or extreme values. A higher IQR indicates more
variability among the middle half of your data.
Consistency of Data: If the IQR is small, the middle 50% of your data
points are relatively close to each other, indicating consistency or less
variability. Conversely, an IQR of 80 suggests that there is a considerable
spread among the middle half of your data.
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 7/41
Variance
THIS IS VERY IMPORTANT!!
The variance is a measure of variability that utilizes all the
data(comparing the variability).
It is based on the difference between
the value of each observation (xi) and the mean (¯x for a sample,µfor a
population).
A great measure of how far each number in a dataset is from the mean
and from every number in the dataset.
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 8/41
Variance
The variance is the average of the squared deviations between each
data value and the mean.
The variance of a sample is:
s 2 =
∑(xi−¯x)2
n−1
The variance for a population is:
σ2 =
∑(xi−µ)2
N
What’s the different betweenn−1 for sample data andN for
population data?
Using n−1 for sample variance corrects for thebias that occurs
because we’re estimating the population mean from a limited sample,
not the entire population.Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 9/41
Variance
Imagine measuring the height of 5 randomly selected people to
estimate the height variance of all people in a city.
If you just use the average of these 5 (which is likely not the true
average of the whole city)
The variance will seem smaller because your average is based on a
limited sample
By dividing byn−1 instead ofn, you’re acknowledging this limitation
and compensating for i
In other words, We divide byn−1 because estimating the mean from
the sample reduces variability, andn−1 corrects this downward bias.
Making your estimate more accurate and less biased towards the small
sample
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 10/41
Standard Deviation
The standard deviation of a data set is the positive square root of the
variance.
It is measured in the same units as the data, making it more easily
interpreted than the variance.
The standard deviation of a sample is:
s =
√
s 2
The standard deviation of a population is:
σ=
√
σ2
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/41
z-score
The z-score is often called thestandardized value.
It denotesthe numberof standard deviations a data valuexi is from
the mean.
An observation’s z-score is a measure of the relative location of the
observation in a data set.
Zi = xi−¯x
s
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 12/41
z-score - examples
Banks use Z-scores to assess the risk of lending. For instance, if the
average credit score in a population is 680 with a standard deviation of
30
A client with a credit score of 740 would have a Z-score of740−680
30 = 2.
This means their score isTWO standard deviations above the mean,
indicating a better-than-average creditworthiness.
Factories use Z-score to measure how far a particular product’s quality
measurement (like the weight, size, or durability) is from the process
mean.
If a production line produces bottles with an average fill of 500ml and a
standard deviation of 5ml, a bottle filled to 510ml would have a Z-score
of 510−500
5 = 2
This can help in identifying products that are outliers and not within the
desired specifications.
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 13/41
z-score
A data value less than the sample mean will have anegative z-score
A data value greater than the sample mean will have apositive z-score
A data value equal to the sample mean will have a z-score of zero.
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 14/41
z-score
Apartment Rents, pick a random rent from the data
Zi = xi−¯x
s = 525−590.8
54.74 =−1.20
Figure 3: Standardized Values for Apartment Rents
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 15/41
Empirical Rule
When the data are believed to approximate a bell-shaped(aka.
symmetrical/normal/gaussian) distribution:
The empirical rule can be used to determine the percentage of data
values that must be within a specified number of standard deviations of
the mean.
The empirical rule is based on the normal distribution, which is covered
in Chapter 6.
For data having a bell-shaped/symmetrical distribution:
Approximately 68% of the data values will be within one standard
deviation of the mean.
Approximately 95% of the data values will be within two standard
deviations of the mean.
Almost all of the data values will be withinthree standard deviations
of the mean.
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 16/41
Empirical Rule
Figure 4: Empirical Rule
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 17/41
Detecting Outliers
An outlier is an unusually small or unusually large value in a data set.
A data value with a z-score less than –3 or greater than +3 might be
considered an outlier.
It might be:
an incorrectly recorded data value
a data value that was incorrectly included in the data set

Box Plot
A box plot is a graphical display of data that is based on a five-number
summary.
Box plots provide another way to identify outliers.
A box is drawn with its ends located at the first and third quartiles.
A vertical line is drawn in the box at the location of the median
(second quartile).
Figure 7: Box Plot for Rents Data
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 24/41
Box Plot
Limits are located using the interquartile range (IQR).
Data outside these limits are considered outliers.
The location of each outlier is shown with the symbol * .
Figure 8: Box Plot w/ Outliers
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 25/41
Box Plot
Example: Apartment Rents
The lower limit is located 1.5(IQR) below Q1.
Lower Limit: Q1 − 1.5(IQR) = 545 − 1.5(80) = 425
The upper limit is located 1.5(IQR) above Q3.
Upper Limit: Q3 + 1.5(IQR) = 625 + 1.5(80) = 745
There are no outliers (values less than 425 or greater than 745) in the
apartment rent data.

Covariance
The covariance is a measure of the linear association between two
variables.
Positive values indicate a positive relationship.
Negative values indicate a negative relationship.
For sample data, the covariance is computed as follows:
Sxy =
∑(xi−¯x)(yi−¯y)
n−1
For population data, the covariance is computed as follows:
σxy =
∑(xi−µx )(yi−µy )
N

Correlation Coefficient
Correlation is a measure of linear association and not necessarily
causation.
Just because two variables are highly correlated, it does not mean that
one variable is the cause of the other.
The correlation coefficient is computed as follows:
For sample:
rxy = sxy
sx sy
For population:
ρxy = σxy
σxσy
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 30/41
Correlation Coefficient
The coefficient can take on values between –1 and +1.
Values near –1 indicate a strong negative linear relationship.
Values near +1 indicate a strong positive linear relationship.
The closer the correlation is to zero, the weaker the relationship.

Coefficient of Variation (CV)
The coefficient of variation (CV) measuresrelative variability.
It standardizes the standard deviation by the mean.
CV is especially useful when comparing datasets withdifferent units
or scales.
CV = s
¯x
# Why Use the Coefficient of Variation?
Standard deviation measuresabsolute risk.
Coefficient of variation measuresrelative risk.
CV answers:
“How risky is this optionrelative to its average level?”
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 36/41
CV Example: Supplier Reliability
Supplier X: Mean delivery = 4 days, SD = 1 day
Supplier Y: Mean delivery = 10 days, SD = 2 days
CVX = 1
4 = 0.25 CVY = 2
10 = 0.20
Supplier X ismore variable relative to its mean, even though it is
faster on average.

Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 40/41
Why CV Matters in Finance
Managers and investors use CV to compare assets with different scales of
returns.
Standard deviationmeasures absolute volatility.
Coefficient of variationmeasures risk per unit of return .
CV tells us how much risk we are taking to earn one unit of return.
A higher CV means more risk for each unit of expected payoff.

Numerical Measures
If the measures are computed for data from a sample, they are called
sample statistics.
What is it?
If the measures are computed for data from a population, they are
called population parameters or population statistics.
What is it?
A sample statistic is referred to as thepoint estimatorof the
corresponding population parameter.
What is it?
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 3/22
Population and Sample
Population
Bigger group or the entire group
All Trinity students
All college students in Texas
All college students in the nation
Sample
Trinity students who are FIN or BAT majored
Trinity students who are taking BAT2301 with Ian in Spring 26
Why Sample vs. Population?
Usually, not practical or even possible to work with the entire population
Thus, we want to use sample data to infer/guess how the population
would “looks” like

Mean
Perhaps the most important measure of location is themean.
The mean provides a measure ofcentral location.
The mean of a data set is the average of all the data values.
The sample mean¯x is the point estimator of the population mean,µ.
¯x =
∑ xi
n
Where ∑ xi = the sum of the values ofn observations and n = the number
of observations in the sample
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 8/22
The Meanings of Some Notations and Greek Letters
∑ = summation of a list of numbers
µrepresents thepopulation mean
¯x represents thesample mean
σrepresents the standard deviation of apopulation
S represents the standard deviation of asample
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 9/22
Discussion
Imagine you manage a sales team, and you want to calculate the
average revenue per salesperson to determine the annual
bonus/commission. Who is a better salesperson?
Not all salespeople have the same number of clients or the same sales
targets.
Some may handle large, high-value clients, while others manage smaller
accounts.
Salesperson A manages 5 clients, contributing a total revenue of $50,000.
Salesperson B manages 15 clients, contributing a total revenue of
$150,000.
Salesperson C manages 10 clients, contributing a total revenue of
$200,000.
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 10/22
Discussion
Can we just find the average revenue per salesperson bydivide the
total revenue by the number of salespeople?
Why or why not?
In this case, using a weighted mean would give you a more accurate
representation of the average revenue per salesperson by taking into
account the size or value of each salesperson’s portfolio.
Let’s use the weighted mean to consider the contribution of each
salesperson based on their number of clients.
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 11/22
Weighted Mean
In some instances the mean is computed by giving each observation a
weight that reflects its relative importance.
The choice of weights depends on the application.
The weights might be the number of credit hours earned for each
grade, as in GPA.
In other weighted mean computations, quantities such as pounds,
dollars, or volume are frequently used.
¯x =
∑ wi xi∑ wi
Where xi = value of observationi, and wi weight got observationi.

Summary About Different Ways to Find the Mean
Simple Mean: you use the simple mean when all data points
contribute equally to the overall picture, like calculating the average
temperature of a city over a week.
Weighted Mean: you use the weighted mean when some data points
are more influential than others, like calculating the average grade in a
class where assignments have different weights or significance.
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 16/22
Percentiles
A percentile provides information about how the data are spread over
the interval from the smallest value to the largest value.
Admission test scores for colleges and universities are frequently
reported in terms of percentiles.
The pth percentile of a data set is a value such that at least p percent
of the items take on this value or less and at least(100 − p) percent of
the items take on this value or more.
Arrange the data in ascending order.
Compute Lp, which is the location of thepth percentile:
Lp = ( p
100)(n +1)
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 17/22
How to Find Percentiles
Figure 5: Percentile Example
Let’s find 80th percentile?
Example: Apartment Rents: Lp = ( p
100 )(n +1) = 80
100 (70 +1) = 56.8
56.8 is a number between 56 and 57
The 80th percentile is the 56th value plus 0.8 times the difference
between the 57th and 56th values.
Thus, the 80th percentile = 635+0.8(649 −635) = 646.2
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 18/22
Interpretations of the Percentiles
Figure 6: Percentile Example
At least 80% of the tenants pay a rent of 646.2 or less.
At least 20% of the tenants pay a rent of 646.2 or more.
Ian Liu Department of Finance and Business Analytics Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 19/22
Quartiles
It’s often desireable to divide a dataset into FOUR parts, with each
part containing approximately 1/4 or 25% of the data points(aka.
observations)
Quartiles are specific percentiles.
First Quartile = 25th Percentile
Second Quartile = 50th Percentile = Median
Third Quartile = 75th Percentile

Why Do We Need Probability?
Managers often base their decisions on an analysis of uncertainties
such as:
What are the chances that the sales will decrease if we increase prices?
What is the likelihood a new assembly method will increase
productivity?
How likely is it that the project will be finished on time?
What is the chance that a new investment will be profitable?

Why Do We Need Probability?

Why Do We Need Probability?
Government agencies and functions often base their decisions on an

a region, and what are the potential costs of disaster response and
recovery?
What are the chances of a budget surplus or deficit by the end of the
fiscal year based on current spending and revenue trends?
How likely is it that government funding for research and development

What is the probability that implementing a new tax will affect

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 7/40
Definitions
Probability is a numerical measure of the likelihood that an event will
occur. Probability values are always assigned on a scale from 0 to 1:
A probability near zero indicates an event is quite unlikely to occur.
A probability near one indicates an event is almost certain to occur.
Other probabilities between 0 and 1 represent degrees of likelihood that
an event will occur.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 8/40
Randomness
Randomness refers to the lack of pattern or predictability in events. A
random sequence of events has no order and does not follow some
pattern or combination.
Rolling a die, flipping a coin, weather patterns, stock market
fluctuations
Want to try the best to have some control over the randomnesses
Probability and statistics are the tools to understand those
randomnesses
Understanding randomness is key to interpreting data, predicting
phenomena, and designing systems in various scientific and practical
fields.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 9/40
Random Experiment
A Random experiment is a process that generates experimental
outcomes, and possesses the following properties
The experimental outcomes are well-defined and may also be listed
prior to conducting the experiment.
On any single repetition (trial) of the experiment, one and only one of
the possible experimental outcomes will occur.
The experimental outcome that occurs on any trial is determined solely
by chance.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 10/40
Statistical Experiments vs. Other Physical Science
Experiments
In statistics, the notion of an experiment differs somewhat from the
notion of an experiment in the physical sciences.
In the physical sciences, researchers usually conduct an experiment in a
laboratory or a controlled environment in order to learn about cause
and effect.
In statistical experiments, probability determines outcomes.
Even though the experiment is repeated in exactly the same way, an
entirely different outcome may occur.
Because of this influence of probability on the outcome, the
experiments of statistics are sometimes called random experiments.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 11/40
Random Experiment and Sample Space
An experimental outcome is also called asample point. The sample
space, S, for an experiment is the set of all experimental outcomes.
Example: consider the random experiment of tossing a coin.
The experimental outcomes (sample points) areHead and Tail.
The sample space is:s ={Head, Tail}
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 12/40
Random Experiment and Sample Space
Now, let’s toss a coin once
What’s the probability of getting the head?
What’s the probability of getting the tail?
What about tossing the coin for 1M times
Record every single experiment result
Aggregate the numbers of tails and heads
Find the means for tail and head
What’s the new probabilities for tail and head?

Counting Rule for Multiple-Step Experiments
A multiple-step experiment can be described as a sequence ofk steps
with n1 possible outcomes on the first step,n2 possible outcomes on
the second step, and so on. (n1,n2,n3, ...,nk)
As an example, consider the random experiment of tossing two coins,
one at a time. The first tossed coin hasn1 = 2 outcomes, and the
second tossed coin has alson2 = 2 outcomes.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 15/40
Counting Rule for Multiple-Step Experiments
From the counting rule, we have:n1∗n2 = 2∗2 = 4 experimental
outcomes
The sample space is:S = (H,H),(H,T ),(T ,H),(T ,T )
The tree diagram for the two-coin toss shown a graphical
representation that helps visualizing a multiple-step experiment.
Figure 1: Tree Diagram for Two-Coin Tossing

points) occur and the project completion time for each outcome.

can compute the probability that the project is completed on time.

Difference Between Combination and Permutation?
Given the letters A, B, C, and D, list the permutations and
combinations for selecting two letters.
Permutation: AB, BA, CA, DA, AC, BC, CB, DB, AD, BD, CD, DC
Combination: AB, BA, CA, DA, AC, BC,CB, DB, AD, BD, CD,DC

Assigning Probabilities
The basic requirements for assigning probabilities are
The probability assigned to each experimental outcome must be
between 0 and 1, inclusively.
The sum of the probabilities for all experimental outcomes must equal
1.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 29/40
Assigning Probabilities
Three methods of assigning probabilities:
The classical method, is based on the assumption of equally likely
outcomes.
The empirical method, based on relative frequencies from experimental
or historical data.
The subjective method, based on experience or intuition when no data
are available.

Events
An event is a collection of sample points.
If we can identify all the sample points of an experiment and assign a
probability to each, we can compute the probability of an event.
1604 Project was an example
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 34/40
Events
Texas DoT was interested in the probability that the project is
completed in 10 months or less.
From the table in the previous slide, we see that there are six sample
points that provide a project completion time of 10 months or less.
Let C denote the event that the project is completed in 10 months or
less. Thus, we have:
C = {(2, 6), (2, 7), (2, 8), (3, 6), (3, 7), (4, 6)}
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 35/40
Events
Some other possible events may be:
L, the event that the project will complete in less than 10 months:
L ={(2,6),(2,7),(3,6)}
M, the event that the project will complete in more than 10 months:
M ={(3,8),(4,7),(4,8)}
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 02/05/2024 36/40
Probability of An Event
The probability of an event is equal to the sum of the probabilities of
the sample points in the event.
We can calculate the probability that the 1604 project is completed in
10 months or lessby adding the probabilities of the six sample
points belonging to eventC.
P(C ) = P(2,6) + P(2,7) + P(2,8) + P(3,6) + P(3,7) + P(4,6)
P(C ) = 0.15 +0.15 +0.05 +0.10 +0.20 +0.05 = 0.7
Similarly, the probability that the 1604 project is completed inless
than 10 monthsis
P(L) = P(2,6) + P(2,7) + P(3,6) = 0.15 +0.15 +0.10 = 0.4
And the probability that the 1604 project is completed inmore than
10 monthsis
P(M) = P(3,8) + P(4,7) + P(4,8) = 0.05 +0.10 +0.15 = 0.3

Some Basic Relationships of Probability
In an experiment with a large number of sample points, the
identification of all the sample points, as well as the determination of
their associated probabilities, can become an extremely cumbersome
task.
In this section, we present some basic probability relationships that
can be used to compute the probability of an event without
knowledge of all the sample point probabilities.
The complement of an event
The union of two events
The intersection of two events
The addition law
The multiplication law

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 1/26
What Is Binomial Distribution? And When To Use
It?
A binomial distributionis a statistical tool to model the number of
successes in a fixed number of trials (or experiments) where each trial
has only two possible outcomes: success or failure.
Think of it as flipping a coin multiple times and counting how many
heads (successes) you get.
Use the binomial distribution when:
You want to model the number of times an event occurs (like getting
heads) in a fixed number of attempts (like flipping a coin).
You’re dealing with situations where there are only two possible
outcomes (success or failure) for each attempt.
You know the probability of success for each trial and want to find out
the likelihood of getting a specific number of successes.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 2/26
Difference Between Uniform Distribution and
Binomial Distribution
Binomial Distribution: Used when you have a fixed number of trials,
each with two possible outcomes (success or failure). You’re
interested in the number of successes.
Example: Flipping a coin 10 times and counting how many heads
(successes) you get.
Uniform Distribution: Used when all outcomes are equally likely.
Every possible outcome has the same probability.
Example: Rolling a fair die, where each of the six faces (1, 2, 3, 4, 5,
or 6) has an equal chance of showing up.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 3/26
The Binomial Experiment
A binomial experiment has the following four properties.
1 The experiment consists of a sequence ofn identical trials.
2 Two outcomes, success and failure, are possible in each trial.
3 The stationarity assumption: the probability of a success, denoted by
p, and the probability of a failure, denoted by 1−p, do not change
from trial to trial.
4 The trials are independent.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 4/26
The Binomial Experiment
Consider the binomial experiment of an insurance agent calling 10
customers.
We define a success if the agent closes the sale of insurance with a
customer, and a failure if he does not.
From past data/experience, we know that the agent closes on an
insurance in 10% of the calls,psuccess = 0.10.
The stationarity assumption requires that the probability of a success
(selling the insurance) remains the same over each trial(call).
The independence of the trials regards the decision of each customer of
whether to purchase or not the insurance.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 5/26
The Binomial Experiment
In a binomial experiment, our interest is in the numberx of successes
occurring in then trials.
Because the number of successes is finite,x is adiscrete random
variable.
The probability distribution associated with this random variable is
called the binomial probability distribution,
And it is described by thebinomial probability function.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 6/26
The Binomial Experiment - Martin Clothing Store
On the basis of past experience, the store manager at the Martin
Clothing store estimates the probability that any one customer will
make a purchase to be 0.30.
What is the probability that two of the next three customers will
make a purchase?
The tree diagram in the next slide shows that the experiment has
eight possible outcomes.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 7/26
The Binomial Experiment - Martin Clothing Store
The requirements for a binomial experiment are met:
Three identical trials, one for each customer entering the store
Two outcomes: S = purchase, F = no purchase
Purchase: p = 0.30; no purchase: 1−p = 0.70
Each purchase decision is independent
Figure 1: 5.5 Martin Clothing Store Problem
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 8/26
The Binomial Probability Function
The binomial probability function determines the probability of
observing x successes in n trials in a binomial experiment.
f (x ) =
(
n
x
)
px (1−p)n−x
Where:
x = the number of successes
p = the probability of a success in one trial
n = the number of trials
f (x ) = the probability ofx successes in n trials
(n
x
)
= n!
x !(n−x )! = the number of experimental outcomes providingx
successes in n trials
px (1−p)n−x provides the probability of a particular sequence of trial
outcomes with x successes in n trials
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 9/26

Clothing Store
Thus, the probability that two (x = 2) of the next three (n = 3)
customers will make a purchase at the Martin Clothing Store is
f (x ) =
(
n
x
)
px (1−p)n−x
f (x ) =
(
3
2
)
0.302(1−0.30)3−2
f (x ) = 2!
(3−2)!0.32(0.7)1
f (x ) = 3×0.063 = 0.189

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 12/26
The Binomial Probability Function
The Binomial Table gives the probability ofx successes in n trials for
a binomial experiment with varying values of the probability of
success: https://uwf.edu/media/university-of-west-
florida/colleges/cse/departments/mathematics-and-
statistics/documents/student-resources/Binomial-Tables-1.pdf
To use the table of binomial probabilities
we must specify the values ofn, p, and x for the binomial experiment
of interest.
For example, to obtain the probability ofx = 3 successes in a binomial
experiment with n = 10 andp = 0.40
First, find the group forn = 10. Second
Second, locate x = 3 from the available rows.
Third, move along the row forn = 10 andx = 3 until you reach the
column corresponding top = 0.40.
The answer is 0.2150.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 13/26
Properties of the Binomial Distribution
In the previous section, we provided formulas for computing the
expected value and variance of a discrete random variable.
If the random variable has a binomial distribution with a known
number of n trials and a knownp probability of success, the general
formulas for the expected value and variance are
E (x ) = µ= np And Var(x ) = σ2 = np(1−p)

Poisson Probability Distribution
A Poisson Probability Distribution describesx, the number of
occurrences over a specified interval of time or space, if the
following two properties of a Poisson experiment are respected
The probability of an occurrence is the same for any two intervals of
equal length.
The occurrence or nonoccurrence in any interval is independent of the
occurrence or nonoccurrence in any other interval.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 17/26
Poisson Probability Distribution
The Poisson probability function is described by the following equation
f (x ) = µx e−µ
x !
Where:
x = a discrete random variable describing the number of occurrences
over an interval.
f (x ) = the probability of x occurrences in an interval
µ= expected value or mean number of occurrences in an interval
NOTE: In a Poisson probability distribution,σ2 = u (the variance is
equal to the mean.)
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 18/26
Poisson Probability Distribution Example
An analysis of historical data shows that patients arrive at the
emergency room of a large hospital on weekend mornings at the
average rateµ=10 over a 15-minute interval.
What is the probability of exactlyx = 5 arrivals in 15 minutes on a
weekend morning?
In a Poisson experiment, we have
f (5) = µx e−µ
x ! = 105e−10
5! = 0.0378 = 3.78%
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 19/26
Poisson Probability Distribution Example
What if we want to know the probability of exactlyx=1 arrival over a
3-minute interval?
We observe that, on average, over a 3-minute interval, we have
µ= 10
15×(3) = 2. Thus, the probability of one arrival over a 3-minute
period is
f (1) = µx e−µ
x ! = 21e−2
1! = 0.2707 = 27.07%
The probability of observing 5 arrivals over a 15-minute period is not
the same as observing 1 arrival over a 3-minute period.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 20/26
Properties of the Poisson Probability Distribution
Because there is no stated upper limit for the number of occurrences,
the Poisson probability functionf (x ) is applicable for valuesx =
0,1,2,... without an upper limit.
In practical applications,x will eventually become large enough so
that f (x ) becomes approximately zero and the probability of any
larger values ofx negligible.
A Poisson probability distribution has the variance equal to the mean:
µ=σ2
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 09/26/2024 21/26
Why Are Mean and Variance the Same for Poisson?
Normally, we know that the variance represents how much the number
of events fluctuates around the mean. In other words, it shows how
much deviation we expect from the average number of occurrences.
For events that following the poisson distribution, rareness and
randomness are being modeled:
Cars speeding is a rare event in the sense that not every car speeds, but
over time, you’ll observe a consistent average.
A speeding car is a rare and random event, which is an independent
event as well.
The number of speeding cars in any given hour is independent of the
number in the previous or next hour (randomness).
That’s why we define them the same.

corresponding toµ= 10.
