Conditional Probability Analysis
We note that the marginal probabilities are found by summing the joint
probabilities in the corresponding row or column of the joint probability
table.
P(A) = P(A∩M) + P(A∩F ) = 0.24 +0.03 = 0.27
The conditional probability that an officer was promotedA given that
the officer is maleM
P(A|M) = P(A∩M)
P(M) = 288/1200
960/1200 = 288
960 = 0.30
Ian Liu Department of Fin&BA Trinity UniversityBAT2301 - Statistics for Business 25/26
Conditional Probability Analysis
The conditional probability that an officer was promotedA given that
the officer is femaleF
P(A|F ) = P(A∩F )
P(F ) = 36/1200
240/1200 = 36
240 = 0.15
Thus, because P(A|M) > P(A|F ), or 0.3 > 0.15, the analysis supports
the female officers’ argument.

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 3/40
Why Interval Estimation?
You don’t want to give an overly confident answer for something you
are not very sure.
It’s like a way of giving a smart guess with a buffer zone, backed with
statistical evidence, knowing you won’t always be 100% precise, but
you’ll be close enough most of the time.
Imagine you’re launching a new product, and you’re trying to guess
how much profit it will make. An interval estimate is like saying, “We
don’t know exactly, but we estimate the profit will be between $50,000
and $80,000.”
You are going out with friends and your parents ask you when you are
gonna be home? Say something-ish, not an exact time.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 4/40
Introduction
A point estimator is a sample statistic used to estimate a population
parameter.
The sample mean¯x is a point estimator of the population meanµ
The sample proportionˆp is a point estimator of the population
proportion p
The sampling distributions of¯x and ˆp play key roles in computing
these interval estimates.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 5/40
Introduction
An interval estimateis computed by adding and subtracting a
value(called the margin of error) to the point estimate. Thus, the
general forms of an interval estimate of a population mean and
proportion are:
¯x ±Margin of Error and ˆp ±Margin of Error
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 6/40
Margin of Error and the Interval Estimate
A point estimatorcannot be expected to provide the exact value of
the population parameter.
But we want to try hard to get closer and closer to the exact
value/truth.
An interval estimatecan be computed by adding and subtracting a
margin of error to the point estimate.
The purpose of an interval estimate is to provide information about
how close the point estimate is to the value of the parameter.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 7/40
Interval Estimate of a Population Mean: When the
σ Is Known
In order to develop an interval estimate of a population mean, the
margin of error must be computed using either:
The population standard deviationσ, or
The sample standard deviations
σis rarely KNOWN exactly(why?). But often a good estimate can be
obtained based on historical data and/or other information available
We refer to such cases as theσKNOWN case
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 8/40

A New Greek Letterα
αis the significance level(or the level of significance) and is used to
calculate a confidence interval(which is often given).
The confidence level is calculated as 100∗(1−α).
It represents the probability of obtaining certain results by chance.

The Confidence Level

estimate ofµusing ¯x±3.92.

include the population mean,µ, but the third one,¯x3, does not.
It turns out that 95% of all intervals formed by subtracting 3.92 from
¯x and adding 3.92 to¯x will include the population mean,µ
We call an interval built around¯x a confidence interval established at
the 95% confidence level.

Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 22/40
Practical Advice(You May Get Asked by An
Interviewer)
Adequate Sample Size
The sampling distribution of¯x is normal if the underlying population
distribution is normal; otherwise, a sample size ofn≥30 is required.
If the population distribution is highly skewed or contains outliers, a
sample size of 50 or more is recommended.
If the population is not normally distributed but is roughly symmetric,
a sample size as small as 15 will suffice.
If the population is believed to be at least approximately normal, a
sample size of less than 15 can be used.
For small sample sizes, a histogram of the sample data should be built
to learn about the shape of the population distribution.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 23/40
Why Interval Estimation?
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=uQo5LhTs6TE
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 24/40
Population Mean: σ Unknown
The t Distribution
If an estimate of the population standard deviation,σ, cannot be
developed prior to sampling, we use the sample standard deviation,s,
instead.
This is referred to as theσunknown case
With the interval estimate ofµbased on thet distribution, which is a
family of similar probability distributions depending on a parameter
called the degrees of freedom.
A t distribution with more degrees of freedom has less dispersion.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 25/40
What is the Degree of Freedom?
Degrees of Freedom refer to the number of independent pieces of
information (data points) that go in the computation of the sample
standard deviation, s, and with thenth data point being “locked” by
the computations of the sample mean,¯x, needed for the computation
of s.
n−1 is how we determine the degree of freedom
Why n−1?
Imagine you’re at a party with a group of friends, and you’ve decided
to line up for a photo. If the photographer asks everyone to spread out
evenly across the frame, the first few friends can choose their spots
freely, but the last friend’s position is determined by everyone else’s
choice to maintain the balance.
In statistics, this is like havingn−1 degrees of freedom: forn friends,
n−1 can choose their spot freely, while the last spot is constrained by
the overall arrangement,n−1 data points are free to vary, but the last
is determined by the sum needed to meet the mean.
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 26/40
Population Mean: σ Unknown
As the degrees of freedom increase, the difference between thet
distribution and the standard normal probability distribution becomes
smaller and smaller
For more than 100 degrees of freedom, the standard normal z value
provides a good approximation to thet value
Keep this in mind: if the degrees of freedom exceed 100, the standard
normal z value provides a good approximation to the t value.
Figure 3: Standard Normal Distribution andt distribution
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 27/40
Interval Estimate ofµ: σ Unknown
An interval estimate of the population meanµ, for theσunknown
case, can be written as
¯x±tα/2
s√n
Where s is the sample standard deviation, 1−αis the confidence
coefficient, and tα/2 is the t value providing an area ofα/2 in the
upper tail of at distribution with n−1 degrees of freedom
Figure 4: t Distribution
Ian Liu Trinity University BAT2301 - Statistics for Business 04/07/2025 28/40

As an application, consider the estimate of the mean credit card debt,
σunknown case, for the population of U.S. households
The data consists of the household credit card debt,x, for a simple
random sample ofn = 70 households.
Sample calculations reveal a sample mean¯x = $9,312, and a sample
standard deviation, s of $4,007.
With 95% confidence level andn−1 = 69 degrees of freedom, we
can use the t-table to obtaint0.025 = 1.995. We want thet value in
the row with 69 degrees of freedom, and the column corresponding to
0.025 in the upper tail.

credit card balance as:
9312±1.9954007√
70 = 9312±955 = [8357,10267]
Where $9,312 is the point estimate of the population mean and $955
the margin of error.
Thus, we are 95% confident that the mean credit card balance for the
population of all households is between $8,357 and $10,267.

Application of Sample Size Determination
A previous study conducted by a TV channel investigated the cost of
renting midsize automobiles and found a mean cost of approximately
$55 per day, with a standard deviation of $9.65. They stated that
they collected a sample of 30 customers who frequently rented
automobiles for travel.
Objective: are their results reliable or statistical valid?
If no, What is the correct sample size to estimate the mean cost of
renting midsize automobiles with a margin of error ofE = $2, a 95%
confidence level, and a planning value for the population standard
deviation, σ=9.65.

A Business Example
In 2017, ABC News reported that 58% of U.S. drivers admit to
speeding. Suppose that a new satellite technology can instantly
measure the speed of any vehicle on a U.S. road and determine
whether the vehicle is speeding, and this satellite technology was used
to take a sample of 20,000 vehicles at 6:00 p.m. EST on a recent
Tuesday afternoon. Of these 20,000 vehicles, 9,252 were speeding.
a. What is the sample proportion of vehicles on U.S. roads that speed?
